тАШрдЙрджреБ рддреНрдпрддреН’ рдЗрддрд┐ рд╖реЛрдбрд╢рд░реНрдЪрдВ рджреНрд╡рд┐рддреАрдпрдВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдореГрдЬрд┐рд╢реНрд╡рди рдЖрд░реНрд╖рдВ рд╡реИрд╢реНрд╡рджреЗрд╡рдореН ред рддреНрд░рдпреЛрджрд╢реНрдпрд╛рджреНрдпрд╛рд╕реНрддрд┐рд╕реНрд░ рдЙрд╖реНрдгрд┐рд╣рдГ рд╖реЛрдбрд╢реНрдпрдиреБрд╖реНрдЯреБрдкреН рд╢рд┐рд╖реНрдЯрд╛рд╕реНрддреНрд░рд┐рд╖реНрдЯреБрднрдГ ред рддрдерд╛ рдЪрд╛рдиреБрдХреНрд░рд╛рдиреНрддрдореН- рдЙрджреБ рддреНрдпрддреНрд╖реЛрд│рд╢ рддреНрд░реНрдпреБрд╖реНрдгрд┐рдЧрдиреБрд╖реНрдЯреБрдмрдиреНрддрдореН ’ рдЗрддрд┐ ред рдЧрддрдГ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╡рд┐рдирд┐рдпреЛрдЧрдГ рее

Jamison Brereton

51 (492)
All Gods
R╠еji┼Ыvan Bh─Бradv─Бja
16 verses: triс╣гс╣нubh 1тАУ12, uс╣гс╣Зih 13тАУ15, anuс╣гс╣нubh 16
This sixteen-verse hymn falls metrically into three quite unequal portions: 1тАУ12, 13тАУ15, and 16. On the basis of both structure and content, it appears that these were originally at least two separate hymns. Verses 1тАУ12 are unitary in tone, and the central, responsive verses 6тАУ7 can be interpreted as an omphalos, supported by various lexical rings. (Oldenberg [1888: 199тАУ200], however, divides these twelve verses into four tr╠еca hymns.)
The hymn so defined differs markedly from the last two All God hymns (VI.49тАУ 50), which catalogue a series of gods and their attributes in an unordered list. This hymn, in contrast, is highly reminiscent of the Mitra, Varuс╣Зa, and S┼лrya hymns in Maс╣Зс╕Нala VII (VII.60тАУ63), in which the Sun surveys the human world and bears wit ness to Mitra and Varuс╣Зa about the innocence and guilt of men. Like those hymns, this begins with the rising of the sun (vss. 1тАУ2); it then turns to praise of the ─Аdityas. The emphasis is on their truth and lack of deceitтАФ─Аdityan preoccupations.

The omphalos verses (6тАУ7), marked by initial repeated m─Б╠Б тАЬdonтАЩt!,тАЭ beg the gods not to subject us to undeserved punishment, thus implicitly claiming our innocence, which should be visible to the all-seeing Sun (though the final p─Бda of the follow ing vs. 8 seems to allow the possibility of a modicum of guilt). The remaining five verses (8тАУ12) return to the theme of the truthful gods, with somewhat more insis tent prayers for grace and help. Toward the end, in verse 11, a larger group of gods is named: invocations of additional gods at the end of a hymn are very common. The last verse (12), naming the priestly family and summarizing the content and intent of the hymn that precedes it, is a typical final verse.
The remaining verses (13тАУ16) may have been appended to this hymn because they chiefly concern various malefactors whom we wish to banish or destroy, including the cheat (rip├║, vs. 13) and the (clearly human) тАЬwolfтАЭ (vr╠е╠Бka, vs. 14), both of which were also mentioned as dangers in the omphalos verses (тАЬcheatтАЭ vs. 7, тАЬwolfтАЭ vs. 6).

English translation:

тАЬThe expansive, illuminating, unobstructive, pure, and beautiful radiance of the sun, grateful to Mitra and Varuс╣Зa, having risen, shines like the ornament of the sky.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Up goes this great eye of Mitra and of Varuс╣ЗaтАФdear and undeceivable. The blazing, sightly face of truth has flashed forth on its rising like the bright ornament of heaven.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The full realization of the dual dvandva mitr─Б╠Б-v├бruс╣З─Б- as two independent dual genitives separated by a p─Бda-break and several words – mitr├бyoс╕е тАж v├бruс╣Зayoс╕е

– is a fine demonstration of the reality of this type of cmpd. in the Sprachgef├╝hl.

I do not understand the p─Бda-final ─Б╠Б(m╠Р). Generally in this position ─Б╠Бfollows an abl., reinforcing the meaning тАЬvon тАж herтАЭ (see Grassmann col. 169), or a loc. But mitr├бyoс╕е is of course not an abl., and, though it could grammatically be a loc., by sense it can only be a gen. It seems pleonastic+++(=redundant)+++ – perhaps added to allow a Triс╣гс╣нubh cadence.

Griffith

THAT mighty eye of Varuna and Mitra, infallible and dear, is moving upward.
The pure and lovely face of holy Order hath shone like gold of heaven in its arising.

Geldner

Da kommt das gro├Яe Auge des Mitra, das liebe, untr├╝gbare des Varuna herauf. Das reine, gern gesehene Bild des Gesetzes ist im Aufgang wie ein Goldschmuck des Himmels aufgeblitzt.

Grassmann

Auf geht dies grosse, holde, unversehrte, das Auge nun des Varuna und Mitra; Des heil’gen helles, sehenswerthes Antlitz, beim Aufgang gl├дnzte wie des Himmels Gold es.

Elizarenkova

рдЕрдзрд┐рдордиреНрддреНрд░рдореН (VC)

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдЕрдм рд╕реЛрд▓рд╣ рдЛрдЪрд╛рд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ рдЗрдХреНрдпрд╛рд╡рдирд╡реЗрдВ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдХрд╛ рдкреНрд░рд╛рд░рдореНрдн рд╣реИ, рдЙрд╕рдХреЗ рдкреНрд░рдердо рдордиреНрддреНрд░ рдореЗрдВ рдлрд┐рд░ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпреЛрдВ рдХреЛ рдХреНрдпрд╛ рдЪрд╛рд╣рдиреЗ рдпреЛрдЧреНрдп рд╣реИ, рдЗрд╕ рд╡рд┐рд╖рдп рдХреЛ рдХрд╣рддреЗ рд╣реИрдВ рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рд╣реЗ рдЕрдзреНрдпрд╛рдкрдХ рдФрд░ рдЙрдкрджреЗрд╢рдХреЛ ! рдЬреЛ рддреБрдо рд▓реЛрдЧреЛрдВ рдХреЛ (рддреНрдпрддреН) рд╡рд╣ рдЙрддреНрддрдо (рдорд╣рд┐) рдмреЬрд╛ рд╡рд╕реНрддреБ рд╡рд╛ (рд╡рд░реБрдгрдпреЛрдГ) рдЙрджрд╛рди рдХреЗ рд╕рдорд╛рди рд╡рд░реНрддреНрддрдорд╛рди рджреЛ рд╕рдЬреНрдЬрдиреЛрдВ рдХрд╛ (рдкреНрд░рд┐рдпрдореН) рдкреНрд░рд┐рдп рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрде рд╡рд╛ (рдорд┐рддреНрд░рдпреЛрдГ) рджреЛ рдорд┐рддреНрд░реЛрдВ рдХрд╛ рдЕрдзреНрдпрд╛рдкрдХ рдФрд░ рдЕрдзреНрдпреЗрддрд╛рдУрдВ рдХрд╛ рд╡рд╛ рд╢рд░реАрд░ рдХреЗ рдмрд╛рд╣рд░ рдФрд░ рднреАрддрд░ рд░рд╣рдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓рд╛ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдг рд╡рд╛рдпреБрдУрдВ рдХрд╛ (рдЕрджрдмреНрдзрдореН) рдЕрд╡рд┐рдирд╖реНрдЯ рд╡реНрдпрд╡рд╣рд╛рд░ рд╡рд╛ (рдЛрддрд╕реНрдп) рд╕рддреНрдп рдХрд╛ (рд╢реБрдЪрд┐) рдкрд╡рд┐рддреНрд░ (рджрд░реНрд╢рддрдореН) рджреЗрдЦрдиреЗ рдпреЛрдЧреНрдп (рджрд┐рд╡рдГ) рдмрд┐рдЬреБрд▓реА рдХреА рдЙрддреНрддреЗрдЬрдирд╛ рд╕реЗ (рдЙрджрд┐рддрд╛) рд╕реВрд░реНрдпреЛрджрдпрдХрд╛рд▓ рдореЗрдВ (рд░реБрдХреНрдордГ) рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд╢рдорд╛рди рд╕реВрд░реНрдп рдХреЗ (рди) рд╕рдорд╛рди (рдЕрдиреАрдХрдореН) рд╕реЗрдирд╛ рд╕рдореВрд╣ рдХреЗ рд╕рдорд╛рди рдХрд╛рд░реНрдпрд╕рд┐рджреНрдзрд┐ рдХрд╛ рдкрд╣реБрдБрдЪрд╛рдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓рд╛ (рдЪрдХреНрд╖реБрдГ) рдЬрд┐рд╕рд╕реЗ рджреЗрдЦрддреЗ рд╣реИрдВ рд╡рд╣ (рд╡рд┐, рдЕрджреНрдпреМрддреН) рд╡рд┐рд╢реЗрд╖рддрд╛ рд╕реЗ рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд╢рд┐рдд рд╣реЛрддрд╛ рд╣реИ (рдЖ, рдЙрддреН, рдПрддрд┐) рдЙрддреНрдХреГрд╖реНрдЯрддрд╛ рд╕реЗ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реЛрддрд╛ рд╣реИ рддреЛ рдЖрдк рд▓реЛрдЧ (рдЙ) рддрд░реНрдХ-рд╡рд┐рддрд░реНрдХ рд╕реЗ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреН рд╣реЛрдУ реерезрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЬреЛ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдп рдзрд░реНрдо рд╕реЗ рдпрд╛рди рдкрд╛рдиреЗ рдХреА рдЗрдЪреНрдЫрд╛ рдХрд░рддреЗ рд╣реИрдВ, рд╡реЗ рд╕реВрд░реНрдп рдХреЗ рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд╢ рдХреЗ рддреБрд▓реНрдп рд╡рд┐рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рди рдХреЛ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реЛрддреЗ рд╣реИрдВ, рдЬреЛ рд╕рддреНрдп рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрде рдХреА рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛ рдХреА рдЙрдиреНрдирддрд┐ рдХрд░рддреЗ рд╣реИрдВ, рд╡реЗ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рддреНрд░ рд╕рддреНрдХреГрдд рд╣реЛрддреЗ рд╣реИрдВ реерезрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рд╣реЗ рдЕрдзреНрдпрд╛рдкрдХреЛрдкрджреЗрд╢рдХрд╛ ! рдпрджрд┐ рдпреБрд╖реНрдорд╛рдВрд╕реНрддреНрдпрдиреНрдорд╣рд┐ рд╡рд░реБрдгрдпреЛрдГ рдкреНрд░рд┐рдпрдВ рдорд┐рддреНрд░рдпреЛрд░рджрдмреНрдзрдореГрддрд╕реНрдп рд╢реБрдЪрд┐ рджрд░реНрд╢рддрдВ рджрд┐рд╡ рдЙрджрд┐рддрд╛ рд░реБрдХреНрдореЛ рдирд╛рд╜рдиреАрдХрдВ рдорд╣рд┐ рдЪрдХреНрд╖реБрд░реНрд╡реНрдпрджреНрдпреМрджрд╛ рдЙрджреЗрддрд┐ рддрд░реНрд╣рд┐ рднрд╡рдиреНрддрд┐ рдЙ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдВрд╕реЛ рднрд╡реЗрдпреБрдГ реерезрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдкреБрдирд░реНрдордиреБрд╖реНрдпреИрдГ рдХрд┐рдореЗрд╖реНрдЯрд╡реНрдпрдорд┐рддреНрдпрд╛рд╣ рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдЙрддреН) (рдЙ) (рддреНрдпрддреН) рддрддреН (рдЪрдХреНрд╖реБрдГ) рдЪрд╖реНрдЯреЗрд╜рдиреЗрди рддрддреН (рдорд╣рд┐) рдорд╣рддреН (рдорд┐рддреНрд░рдпреЛрдГ) рд╕реБрд╣реГрджреЛрд░рдзреНрдпрд╛рдкрдХрд╛рд╜рдзреНрдпреЗрддреНрд░реЛрд░реНрдмрд╛рд╣реНрдпрд╛рднреНрдпрдиреНрддрд░рд╕реНрдердпреЛрдГ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдгрдпреЛрд░реНрд╡рд╛ (рдЖ) (рдПрддрд┐) (рдкреНрд░рд┐рдпрдореН) рдпрддреНрдкреНрд░реАрдгрд╛рддрд┐ рддрддреН (рд╡рд░реБрдгрдпреЛрдГ) рдЙрджрд╛рди рдЗрд╡ рд╡рд░реНрддреНрддрдорд╛рдирдпреЛрдГ (рдЕрджрдмреНрдзрдореН) рдЕрд╣рд┐рдВрд╕рд┐рддрдореН (рдЛрддрд╕реНрдп) рд╕рддреНрдпрд╕реНрдп (рд╢реБрдЪрд┐) рдкрд╡рд┐рддреНрд░рдореН (рджрд░реНрд╢рддрдореН) рджреНрд░рд╖реНрдЯрд╡реНрдпрдореН (рдЕрдиреАрдХрдореН) рд╕реИрдиреНрдпрдорд┐рд╡ рдХрд╛рд░реНрдпрд╕рд┐рджреНрдзрд┐рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкрдХрдореН (рд░реБрдХреНрдордГ) рд░реЛрдЪрдорд╛рдирд╕реНрд╕реВрд░реНрдпрдГ (рди) рдЗрд╡ (рджрд┐рд╡рдГ) рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпреБрддрдГ рд╕рдХрд╛рд╢рд╛рддреН (рдЙрджрд┐рддрд╛) рд╕реВрд░реНрдпреНрдпреЛрджрдпреЗ (рд╡рд┐) (рдЕрджреНрдпреМрддреН) рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд╢рдпрддрд┐ реерезрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдпреЗ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпрд╛рдГ рдзрд░реНрдореЗрдг рдпрд╛рдирдВ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрддреБрдорд┐рдЪреНрдЫрдиреНрддрд┐ рддреЗ рд╕реВрд░реНрдпрдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд╢рд╡рддреНрдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрддрд╡рд┐рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдирд╛ рдЬрд╛рдпрдиреНрддреЗ рдпреЗ рд╕рддреНрдпрд╕реНрдп рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╕реНрдп рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рдореБрдиреНрдирдпрдиреНрддрд┐ рддреЗ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рддреНрд░ рд╕рддреНрдХреГрддрд╛ рднрд╡рдиреНрддрд┐ реерезрее

рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛ рдЬреЛрд╢реА тЖР рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рдо) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдпрд╛ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╛рдд рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡реЗрджреЗрд╡рд╛рдЪреНрдпрд╛ рдХрд░реНрдорд╛рдЪреЗ рд╡рд░реНрдгрди рдЕрд╕рд▓реНрдпрд╛рдореБрд│реЗ рдпрд╛ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╛рдЪреНрдпрд╛ рдЕрд░реНрдерд╛рдЪреА рдкреВрд░реНрд╡ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдмрд░реЛрдмрд░ рд╕рдВрдЧрддреА рдЬрд╛рдгрд╛рд╡реА.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬHe who knows the three cognizable (worlds); the sage (who knows) the mysterious birth of the divinities (abiding in them); he who is beholding the good and evil acts of mortals, he, the sun, the lord, makes manifest their intentions.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The divinities abiding in them: Of the Vasus on earth, the Rudras in the firmament, the ─Аdityas in heaven. Vasus are the ’earthly riches’; the other divinities are ‘instrumental uments’ in the process of making wealth

Jamison Brereton

The inspired poet who knows their three divisions and the breeds of the gods far away and here,
who sees the straight and the crooked among mortals, the Sun looks upon the ways of the stranger.

Jamison Brereton Notes

vid├бtha- is here not тАШceremony of division, riteтАЩ, but rather тАШdivisionтАЩ itself, referring to the divisions of the gods. Geldner aptly adduces VI.52.15 in the next hymn, where the gods are born in 3 different localities.

Oldenberg strenuously objects to taking sanut├бr ─Б╠Бca as a conjoined phrase of directional elements (flg. BR), and Renou agrees with him. I do not see the problem; ─Б╠Бis of course generally a preverb and less commonly an adposition, but in these usages it is clearly directional/locational, and conjoining it with another such element seems well within RVic syntactic bounds, even if the other word is more clearly adverbial.

Moreover, neither Oldenberg nor Renou gives any indication of what to do with ca if itтАЩs not conjoining the two. I therefore follow Geldner (flg. BR) and Klein (DGRV I.63). (The case of Renou is a bit complex: he expresses his objections to the BR view in the notes to the Vi┼Ыvedev─Бс╕е hymns in EVP IV, but in the tr. of those same hymns in EVP V he tr.

as a conjoined phrase тАЬau loin et au pr├иs.тАЭ Either he forgot or he changed his mind.)

Griffith

The Sage who knows these Gods’ three ranks and orders, and all their generations near and distant,
Beholding good and evil acts of mortals, Sura marks well the doing of the pious.

Geldner

Der die dreifache Kunde von ihnen und der G├╢tter Geschlechter kennt, der Kundige schaut nach jenseits und herw├дrts. Indem er das Rechte und Falsche in den Menschen schaut, nimmt der Sonnengott die W├╝nsche des hohen Herrn wahr.

Grassmann

Der Sonnengott, der die drei G├╢tterscharen und ihren Ursprung kennet fern und nahe, Der Recht und Unrecht bei den Menschen schauet, hat sorgsam Acht auf des Gerechten Pfade.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬI praise you, protectors of the solemn sacrifice, the well-born Aditi, Mitra and Varuс╣Зa and Aryaman and Bhaga; I celebrate the gods whose acts are unimpeded, the bestowers of wealth, the dispensers of purity.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

I will praise you, the great herdsmen of truth: Aditi, Mitra, Varuс╣Зa, the well-born ones.
Aryaman, Bhaga, those of undeceivable inspired thoughts, the pure companions, do I call here.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The opening of this vs., stuс╣г├й, is identical to the beginning of VI.49 and very similar to the beginning of VI.50 (huv├й), both of which vss. (VI.49.1, VI.50.1) contain the divine list discussed in the next paragraph.

We have already had occasion to note (comm. ad VI.49.1, 50.1) the unexpected trio Varuс╣Зa, Mitra, Agni, in which Agni substitutes for expected Aryaman. Here we have a different third member: Aditi, Mitra, Varuс╣Зa (├бditim mitr├бс╣Г v├бruс╣Зam), opening rather than closing the p─Бda. Of course, as their mother, Aditi has a closer connection to Mitra and Varuс╣Зa than Agni does, but in fact she is rarely found in their immediate company: only in the voc. phrase II.27.14 ├бdite m├нtra v├бruс╣Зot├б also p─Бda-init. and in a larger list of gods in V.46.3. In our passage the missing Aryaman is added at the beginning of the next p─Бda (3c), just as he was added in the p─Бda (c) immediately following the list in VI.50.1b. Note that in VI.50.1 ├бditim precedes the trio in the first p─Бda of the vs. (VI.50.1a).

In p─Бda a I take mah├бс╕е as an acc. pl., contra the standard tr. (Geldner, Renou, Scarlatta 291) тАЬherdmen of great truth.тАЭ Either is of course grammatically and semantically possible, but I was influenced by the undoubted acc. pl. mah├бс╕е also referring to the gods in the next vs. (4b) as well as 9d.

The vaс╕е in p─Бda a is ambig. With the standard tr. (Geldner, Renou, Scarlatta 291), I take it as referring to the gods in the 2nd ps. On the other hand, references to the gods have so far been in the 3rd ps. and will remain so in the next vs.; 2nd ps. address only appears in vs. 5. So it would be equally possible to take vaс╕е as an instance of the common practice of a poet addressing his priestly comrades, тАЬI will praise, for you/on your behalf, the great herdsmen of truth тАжтАЭ Nothing much hangs on the difference, nor is there any way to determine which is correct.

Note that ├бdabdha-dh─лt─лn тАШhaving undeceivable inspired thoughtsтАЩ at the end of c echoes ├бditim beginning b, despite the differences in lexicon and even segmentation. It also is responsive with с╣Ыt├б-dh─лtayaс╕е тАШhaving truth as inspired thoughtsтАЩ in 10d, and the two form part of the ring around the omphalos vss. 6-7.

While ├бdabdha- is taken up by ├бdabdh─Бn in 4a.

For sadhany├ас╕е I now favor the scenario sketched by Scarlatta (291) as an alternative to the analysis as belonging to a root noun cmpd. sadha-n─л╠Б-. See comm. ad IV.1.9. As noted there, Scarlatta begins with a sa-dh├бna- тАШcommon wealthтАЩ to which a

*sadhan├н- тАШsharer in common wealthтАЩ ├а тАШcompanionтАЩ could be formed. He then suggests that because of a perceived connection with тИЪn─л, the stem was reinterpreted and reformed as sadhan─л╠Б-. Although this requires more machinery than simply taking it as a root noun cmpd. to тИЪn─л in the first place, the semantics of that supposed cmpd.

are somewhat troublesome; moreover the stem sadhanitv├б- can be more easily derived by this route. Michael Weiss alternatively suggests that the stem is a vс╣Ыk─л deriv. to sadh├бna-. This would account for the morphology more easily that what was just sketched; however, it would have to be masc. vс╣Ыk─л form. Not impossible of course (cf. rath─л╠Б-), but one more required assumption.

Aryaman, Bhaga, all whose thoughts are faithful: hither I call the Bright who share in common.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe scatterers of the malevolent, the defenders of the virtuous, the irresistible, the mighty lords, the donors of good dwellings, ever young, very powerful, omnipresent, leader of heaven, the sons of ─Аditya; I have recourse to Aditi, who is gratified by mine adoration.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Those who care for the stranger, the lords of settlements, undeceivable, the great kings, givers of good dwelling,
the youths of good rule ruling over Heaven, the superior menтАФthe
─Аdityas I beseech and Aditi, in quest of friendship.

Jamison Brereton Notes

I follow Geldner (as well as Thieme Fremdling, Oberlies I.344, etc.) in rendering suvasan├б- as тАШgood dwellingтАЩ, against some potentially good arguments to the contrary. The stem is attested only once elsewhere, IX.97.50 in the phrase v├бstr─Б suvasan─Б╠Бni, where it clearly refers to good garments (тИЪvas тАШwear, clotheтАЩ), and the base of our cmpd, v├бsana- (a hapax), likewise only means clothing. Citing these words, as well as vastra-d─Б╠Б- тАШgiving garmentsтАЩ (V.42.8; like our phrase suvasan├бsya d─Бtс╣Ы╠Д╠Бn), Renou holds firm to тАЬdonateurs de bonne v├кtureтАЭ (so also Grassmann). But s├бtpat─лn тАШlords of settlementsтАЩ in the preceding p─Бda supports a тАШdwellingтАЩ interpr., and it would be easy to form such a deriv. to the well-attested root тИЪvas тАШdwellтАЩ. (Note that the derivatives that would support the тАШclothingтАЩ sense are found in that sense only once apiece, so do not seem well established enough to block such a formation.) Geldner construes div├бс╕е with nс╣Ы╠Д╠Бn and take kс╣г├бyataс╕е absolutely: тАЬdie m├дchtigen Herrn des Himmels.тАЭ As in vs. 2, Renou seems to have changed his mind (a phenomenon I know well; witness this comm.) between the comm. fascicle (EVP IV) and the tr.

fascicle (EVP V): in the former he comments of kс╣г├бyataс╕е тАЬemploi absolu,тАЭ but in the latter tr. тАЬseigneurs r├йsidants du ciel,тАЭ with div├бс╕е dependent on the participle. He evidently assigns the participle to тАШdwellтАЩ, though the participle of the root pres. to that root is only kс╣гiy├бnt-, while kс╣г├бyant- belongs to kс╣г├бya- тАШrule overтАЩ. (Curiously he correctly interpr. the finite kс╣г├бyatha in 7c as тАЬvous r├йgnez.тАЭ) Geldner (etc.) must base their interpr. on the existence of the phrase div├│ n├бraс╕е / nс╣Ы╠Д╠Бn, but though this collocation is attested elsewhere (e.g., V.54.10, VI.2.3, VI.2.11=14.6), it is not a particularly common expression, and тИЪkс╣гi тАШrule overтАЩ regularly takes a genitive, incl. in 7c v├н┼Ыvasya h├н kс╣г├бyatha тАЬfor you rule over all,тАЭ a phrase Renou in fact cites in his comm. _________ 05
This vs. consists primarily of a string of vocatives, plus a couple of 2nd pl.

impvs., so in one way it is quite straightforward. However, the accentual behavior of the vs., and particularly the vocc., is peculiar. The first p─Бda consists only of vocatives: two double names (Father Heaven, Mother Earth) and a single adjective (by word order belonging to the latter, but it is a root noun cmpd and its voc. is indifferent to gender). Each word in the p─Бda is accented (with voc. accent): dya├╣с╣г p├нtaс╕е pс╣Ы╠Бthivi m─Б╠Бtar ├бdhruk. The first three words of the next p─Бda are likewise vocatives: a name plus epithet and a different (pl.) name. Only the first of these is accented: ├бgne bhr─Бtar vasavaс╕е. The next word is an impv. mс╣Ыс╕╖├бt─Б, and it is accented after the extrasentential voc. phrase (cf. comm. ad VI.50.11, where this was floated as a possibility to explain an unusually accented verb [the same verb in fact], though rejected). The third p─Бda also begins with three vocatives, one a two-word phrase, one an individual name, with only the first accented: v├н┼Ыva ─Бdity─Б adite. I am completely puzzled as to why the first p─Бda differs from the next two. Oldenberg is also puzzled: тАЬBehandlung der Vokativakzente befremdet, aber wir haben kein Recht zu r├╝hren.тАЭ The content of the vs. is otherwise banal. рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рд░рд┐рд╢рд╛рджрд╕рдГ) рд╣рд┐рдВрд╕рдХрд╛рдиреН рдирд╛рд╢рдХрд╛рдиреН (рд╕рддреНрдкрддреАрдиреН) рд╕рддреНрдпрд╕реНрдп рдкрд╛рд▓рдХрд╛рдиреН (рдЕрджрдмреНрдзрд╛рдиреН) рдЕрд╣рд┐рдВрд╕рд┐рддрд╛рдирд╣рд┐рдВрд╕рдХрд╛рдиреН (рдорд╣рдГ) рдорд╣рддрдГ (рд░рд╛рдЬреНрдЮрдГ) рдиреГрдкрд╛рдиреН (рд╕реБрд╡рд╕рдирд╕реНрдп) рд╕реБрд╖реНрдареБрд╡рд╛рд╕рд╕реНрдп (рджрд╛рддреДрдиреН) (рдпреВрдирдГ) рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрддрдпреМрд╡рдирд╛рдиреН (рд╕реБрдХреНрд╖рддреНрд░рд╛рдиреН) рдЙрддреНрддрдордзрдирд╛рдЮреНрдЫреНрд░реЗрд╖реНрдард░рд╛рдЬреНрдпрд╛рдиреН рд╡рд╛ (рдХреНрд╖рдпрддрдГ) рдирд┐рд╡рд╕рддрдГ (рджрд┐рд╡рдГ) рдХрдордиреАрдпрд╛рдиреН рдХрд╛рдордпрдорд╛рдирд╛рдиреН рд╡рд╛ (рдиреДрдиреН) (рдЖрджрд┐рддреНрдпрд╛рдиреН) рдХреГрддрд╛рд╖реНрдЯрдЪрддреНрд╡рд╛рд░рд┐рдВрд╢рджреН[рд╡рд░реНрд╖]рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдордЪрд░реНрдпреЗрдг рдкреВрд░реНрдгрд╡рд┐рджреБрд╖рдГ (рдпрд╛рдорд┐) рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдиреЛрдорд┐ (рдЕрджрд┐рддрд┐рдореН) рдЕрдЦрдгреНрдбрд┐рддрд╛рдВ рдиреАрддрд┐рдореН (рджреБрд╡реЛрдпреБ) рджреБрд╡рдГ рдкрд░рд┐рдЪрд░рдгрдВ рдХрд╛рдордпрдорд╛рдирд╛рдиреН реерекрее

English translation:

тАЬFather Heaven, innocent mother Earth, brother Agni, and you, Vasus, grant us happiness; all you sons of Aditi, and you Aditi, alike well-plural ased, bestow upon us ample felicity.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

O Father Heaven, Mother Earth lacking the lie, Brother Agni, good onesтАФhave mercy on us.
All you ─Аdityas and Aditi jointlyтАФspread out ample shelter for us.

Griffith

O Heaven our Father, Earth our guileless Mother, O Brother Agni, and ye Vasus, bless us.
Grant us, O Aditi and ye Adityas, all of one mind, your manifold protection.

Geldner

Grassmann

O Vater Himmel, treue Mutter Erde, o Bruder Agni, seid uns hold, ihr guten, Aditja’s ihr und Aditi vereinigt, o reichet alle ausgedehnten Schutz uns.

English translation:

тАЬSubject us not, adorable (deities), to the robber or his wife; not to any one designing us harm; for you are the regulators of our person ns, of our strength, of our speech.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

To the robber: m─Б no vс╣Ыk─Бya vс╣Ыkye r─лradhat─Б: hiс╣Гsak─Бya, sten─Бya, to the injurer, the thief; tasya stiyai, to his woman or wife; vс╣Ыka may mean wild-dog or wolf, araс╣Зya ┼Ыv─Бn; vс╣Ыki is a feminine le wolf

Jamison Brereton

DonтАЩt make us subject to the wolf, to the she-wolf, to any at all who wishes us ill, o you who deserve the sacrifice,
for you are the charioteers of our bodies and you have become (the
charioteers) of (our?) skillful speech.

Jamison Brereton Notes

P─Бda d must remain in the domain of h├н in c, as shown by the accent on babh┼лv├б, as is recognized by the standard tr.

The repetition of y┼лy├бm at the beginning of d is, I think, due not only to rhetoric but to the desire to make the ps./no. of babh┼лv├б perfectly clear. The 2nd pl.

act. pf. is surely the least well attested form of the act. perfect system (save for 1st du.), and it also has a highly under-characterized ending (-a), which has the misfortune to be identical to the ending of the best attested form in the pf. system, the 3rd sg., as well as the less well attested 1st sg. (For the relative strengths of attestation, a glance at MacdonellтАЩs Vedic Grammar ┬з485 will suffice.) In most pf. paradigms it would be distinguished from those forms by ablaut grade (e.g., 1st sg. cak├бra, 3rd sg.

cak─Б╠Бra, 2nd pl. cakr├б), but here, because the pf. of тИЪbh┼л doesn’t ablaut, only the accent separates it from 3rd (and 1st) sg. babh┼л╠Бva. This may be another reason that it was kept syntactically in the realm of h├н, to require it to have an accent. ItтАЩs worth noting that this is the only 2nd pl. pf. to тИЪbh┼л in the RV.

d├бkс╣гa- is ordinarily a noun, тАШskillтАЩ, but in the published translation I was persuaded by the standard tr. to render it as an adj. тАШskillfulтАЩ with v├бcas-. This phrase also occurs in VIII.86.1 and, with a different derivative of тИЪvac, in X.113.9 d├бkс╣гebhir vacan├йbhiс╕е.

In the latter I tr. as an adj. тАЬwith skillful words,тАЭ but in the former as two independent nouns тАЬof skill and of speech.тАЭ I am uncertain which is correct. Renou is quite stern: тАЬd├бkс╣гa- est n├йcessairement adjectif ici et en plusieurs passages тАж: inutile de chercher ├а ├йviter ici lтАЩemploi, avec Grassmann, emploi qui est le seul subsistant en skt cl.тАЭ The Classical Skt. usage is suggestive, but I am wary of the absolutist language of тАЬn├йcessairementтАЭ and тАЬinutileтАЭ: very few things in RVic interpr. are absolutely necessary. I would therefore allow an alt. tr. here: тАЬyou have become (the charioteers) of (our) skill and speech.тАЭ That vs. 9 contains a cmpd. containing the noun, p┼лt├б-dakс╣гa- тАШof refined skillтАЩ, though modifying the gods, might support a тАШskillтАЩ interpr. here, esp. as the тАШcharioteerтАЩ motif is found there as well.

Griffith

Give us not up to any evil creature, as spoil to wolf or she-wolf, O ye Holy.
For ye are they who guide aright our bodies, ye are the rulers of our speech and vigour.

рд╣реЗ рджреЗрд╡рд╛рдГ рд╡рдГ рдпреБрд╖реНрдорд╛рдХрдВ рд╕реНрд╡рднреВрддрд╛ рд╡рдпрдореН рдЕрдиреНрдпрдХреГрддрдореН рдЕрдиреНрдпреИрдГ рд╢рддреНрд░реБрднрд┐рдГ рдХреГрддрдореБрддреНрдкрд╛рджрд┐рддрдореН рдПрдирдГ рдкрд╛рдкрдВ рдорд╛ рднреБрдЬреЗрдо рдорд╛ рднреБрдВрдХреНрд╖реНрдорд╣рд┐ ред рд╣реЗ рд╡рд╕рд╡рдГ рд╡рд╛рд╕рдпрд┐рддрд╛рд░реЛ рджреЗрд╡рд╛рдГ рдпрддреН рдпреЗрди рдХреГрддреЗрди рдкрд╛рдкреЗрди рдЪрдпрдзреНрд╡реЗ рдЕрд╕реНрдорд╛рдиреН рдмрд╛рдзрдзреНрд╡реЗ ред рдЪрдпрддрд┐рд░реНрд╣рд┐рдВрд╕рд╛рдХрд░реНрдорд╛ ред рддрддреН рдЪ рдкрд╛рдкрдВ рдорд╛ рдХрд░реНрдо рдорд╛ рдХрд╛рд░реНрд╖реНрдо рее рдХрд░реЛрддреЗрд░реНрдорд╛рдЩрд┐ рд▓реБрдЩрд┐ тАШрдордиреНрддреНрд░реЗ рдШрд╕’ рдЗрддрд┐ рдЪреНрд▓реЗрд░реНрд▓реБрдХреН рее рд╣реЗ рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рджреЗрд╡рд╛рдГ рд╕рд░реНрд╡реЗ рджреЗрд╡рд╛рдГ рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рд╕реНрдп рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╕реНрдп рдЬрдЧрддреЛ рдпреВрдпрдВ рд╣рд┐ рдХреНрд╖рдпрде рдИрд╢реНрд╡рд░рд╛ рднрд╡рде ред рдЕрддрдГ рдХрд╛рд░рдгрд╛рддреН рдЕрд╕реНрдорджреАрдпрдГ рд░рд┐рдкреБрдГ рд╢рддреНрд░реБрдГ рддрдиреНрд╡рдВ рд╕реНрд╡рд╢рд░реАрд░рдВ рд╕реНрд╡рдпрдореН рдПрд╡ рд░рд┐рд░рд┐рд╖реАрд╖реНрдЯ рд╣рд┐рдВрд╕реНрдпрд╛рддреН ред рдпрдереИрд╡рдВ рднрд╡рддрд┐ рддрдерд╛ рдХреБрд░реБрддреЗрддрд┐ рднрд╛рд╡рдГ рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬLet us not suffer for the sin committed by another; let us not do that which, Vasus, you prohibit; you rule universal gods, over the universe; (so provide that) mine enemy may inflict injury on his own person n.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

DonтАЩt let us pay for the offense done to you by another; donтАЩt let us do that which you avenge, o good ones,
for you rule over all, All Gods. Let the cheat harm his own body.

On apparently anomalous m─Б╠БтАж bhujema see comm. ad IV.3.13.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬReverence be to the potent (company of universal gods); I offer (them) reverence; reverence sustains both earth and heaven; revernce be to the gods; reverence is sovereign over them; I expiate by reverence whatever sin may have been committed.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Reverence sustains: earth and heaven, by receiving namas or namask─Бra, the reverential salutation or homage of mortals, continue throughout a long period for their enjoyment

Jamison Brereton

Reverence is powerful. I seek to attract reverence here. Reverence upholds heaven and earth.
Reverence to the gods; reverence is master of them. With reverence
I seek to redeem even an offense committed.

Jamison Brereton Notes

In this deliberately repetitive vs. (6 occurrences of n├бmas-), it is difficult to render the repeated verbs ─Б╠Бvivase (a, d) in the same way. As the desid. to тИЪvan, viv─Бsa-, esp. with ─Б╠Б, means lit. тАШseek to win hereтАЩ, hence тАШattractтАЩ, which is fine in p─Бda a. But with the object тАЬcommitted offenseтАЭ (kс╣Ыt├бm ├йnaс╕е) the sense is harder to manipulate. I take it as тАШwin backтАЩ, hence тАШredeemтАЩ; Geldner тАШabbittenтАЩ (beg pardon, apologize), with no attempt to connect this tr. to the literal meaning or to the other occurrence of the verb in the passage; Renou makes good use of his usual parentheses: тАЬje lтАЩattire (pour le d├йtruire),тАЭ which evades the problem.

Griffith

Mighty is homage: I adopt and use it. Homage hath held in place the earth and heaven.
Homage to Gods! Homage commands and rules them. I banish even committed sin by homage

Geldner

Die Anbetung ist m├дchtig, die Anbetung bitte ich her. Die Anbetung erh├дlt Erde und Himmel. Anbetung geb├╝hrt den G├╢ttern, die Anbetung hat ├╝ber sie Macht. Auch die getane S├╝nde bitte ich durch Anbetung ab.

Grassmann

Gebet ist m├дchtig, das Gebet gewinn’ ich, Gebet hielt fest den Himmel und die Erde; Gebet den G├╢ttern! das Gebet beherrscht sie, begangne Schuld auch tilge durch Gebet ich.

тАЬAdorable (deities), I venerate with reverential salutations all you who are mighty, the mighty, the regulators of your sacrifice, of pure vigour, dwellers in the chamber of worship, unsubdued, far-seeing, leaders (of rites).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The regulator: с╣Ыtasya rathyaс╕е = yaj├▒asya ranhitс╣Ыn, netс╣Ыn, leaders or conveyers of the sacrifice offered to them

Jamison Brereton

You charioteers of truth who possess refined skill, settled in the dwelling places of truth, undeceivable,
all you great superior men of broad gaze do I bend here with
reverences, o you who deserve the sacrifice.

Jamison Brereton Notes

This vs. recalls the n├бmas- vs. (8), with its two occurrences of ─Б╠Бvivase, one of which is construed with instr. n├бmas─Б. Here we have the verb form ─Б╠Бname, which imitates ─Б╠Бvivase in preverb and med. 1st sg. form, but with the verbal root from which n├бmas- is derived, тИЪnam тАШbow, bendтАЩ. It also is construed with an instr. of the s-stem, n├бmobhiс╕е.

Griffith

You Furtherers of Law, pure in your spirit, infallible, dwellers in the home of Order,
To you all Heroes mighty and far-seeing I bow me down, O Holy Ones, with homage.

Geldner

Euch, die Lenker des Gesetzes von lauterem Wollen, die im Hause des Gesetzes wohnen, die untr├╝glichen, diese weitschauenden M├дnner, euch alle, die Gro├Яen, mache ich durch Anbetung geneigt, ihr Opferw├╝rdige.

Grassmann

Euch reingesinnte Lenker heil’gen Brauches, des heil’gen Brauches treue Hausgenossen, Euch bet’ ich an, die weithinschaunden alle, mit Demuth euch, die hohen, hehren M├дnner.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay they, exceeding in splendour, so guide us, that all iniquities may disappear, they, the very powerful Varuс╣Зa, Mitra, Agni, practisers of truth, and faithful to those who are prominent in (their) praise.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

For they possess the best luster and they lead us across all difficultiesтАФ those of good rule, Varuс╣Зa, Mitra, Agni, whose inspired thoughts are truth, who are in reality rulers of speech.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Judging from the repeated t├й and the u that follows the 2nd one (strikingly in the middle of a p─Бda), we should be dealing with two parallel clauses, one nominal, one verbal. The accent on n├бyanti shows that the 2nd clause is in the domain of the h├н in p─Бda a. Geldner renders as two clauses, but does not seem to keep the 2nd in the h├н domain; Renou ignores the t├й u and tr. as a single clause. There does not appear to be a main clause in the vs., unless we want to construe cd as a nominal main cl. (тАЬthey are of good rule тАжтАЭ).

sukс╣гatr├б- reprises the same word in 4c, and as noted ad vs. 3, с╣Ыt├б-dh─лtimatches ├бdabdha-dh─лti in 3c. The two are part of the supportive ring around the omphalos vss. 6-7.

Once again we meet the trio Varuс╣Зa, Mitra, Agni (see comm. on vs. 3, and previous vss. noted there), but Aryaman is nowhere in the vicinity and Aditi only in a rather random list in the next vs. (11).

Consonant with the focus on truth in this hymn, p─Бda d is framed by the words с╣Ыt├б- and saty├б-, the former as first member of a cmpd, the latter as last member. As was just noted, с╣Ыt├б-dh─лti- is a well-formed bahuvr─лhi with a parallel already in the hymn. But vakma-r─Б╠Бja-satya- is distinctly peculiar. For one thing, it has three members, which is unusual for the RV. But more striking is the final member satya-, whose relation to the prior (complex) member vakma-r─Б╠Бja(n)- is unclear. (Curiously, AiG doesnтАЩt touch this cmpd.) Its only possible parallel is the even stranger с╣Ыt├б-j─Бta- satya-, with both с╣Ыt├б- and saty├б-, in IV.51.7 (see comm. ad loc.). Grassmann glosses тАЬdem Lenker der Gebete treu oder willf├дhrig.тАЭ Geldner treats as two separate words тАЬ‘die beredten K├╢nige, die wahrhaften,тАЭ without commenting on this disjunction (or does he think itтАЩs a dvandva?), though he cites S─Бyaс╣Зa. as interpr. тАЬwahrhaftig gegen die Herren der Rede d.h. die S├дnger,тАЭ which is also reflected in GrassmannтАЩs gloss. OldenbergтАЩs тАЬin Wahrheit K├╢nige der RedeтАЭ and RenouтАЩs тАЬqui sont vraiment les rois de la parole (sacrale)тАЭ are in essential agreement, and the published translation follows them – though I feel as though weтАЩre all missing something.

Griffith

рддреЗ рджреЗрд╡рд╛рдГ рдирдГ рдЕрд╕реНрдорд╛рдХрдВ рдХреНрд╖рд╛рдо рдирд┐рд╡рд╛рд╕рднреВрдорд┐рдВ рд╡рд░реНрдзрдиреН рд╡рд░реНрдзрдпрдиреНрддреБ ред рдХреЗ рддреЗред рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рдГ рдкреГрдерд┐рд╡реА рдЪ рдкреВрд╖рд╛ рдЪ рднрдЧрдГ рдЪ рдЕрджрд┐рддрд┐рдГ рдЕрджреАрдирд╛ рджреЗрд╡рдорд╛рддрд╛ рдЪ рдкрдЮреНрдЪ рдЬрдирд╛рдГ тАШрджреЗрд╡рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпрд╛рдгрд╛рдВ рдЧрдиреНрдзрд░реНрд╡рд╛рдкреНрд╕рд░рд╕рд╛рдореН’ ( рдР. рдмреНрд░рд╛. рей. рейрез ) рдЗрддреНрдпрд╛рджрд┐рдмреНрд░рд╛рд╣реНрдордгреЛрдХреНрддрд╛ рджреЗрд╡рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпрд╛рджрдпрд╢реНрдЪ рддреЗ рдЪ рдирдГ рдЕрд╕реНрдорджрд░реНрдердВ рд╕реБрд╢рд░реНрдорд╛рдгрдГ рд╕реБрд╕реБрдЦрд╛рдГ рд╕реНрд╡рд╡рд╕рдГ рд╢реЛрднрдирд╛рдиреНрдирд╛рдГ рд╕реБрдиреАрдерд╛рдГ рд╕реБрдкреНрд░рд╛рдкрдгрд╛рд╢реНрдЪ рднрд╡рдиреНрддреБ ред рдЕрд╕реНрдорднреНрдпрдВ рд╢реЛрднрдирд╕реБрдЦрд╛рджрд┐рдХрдВ рдкреНрд░рдпрдЪреНрдЫрдиреНрддреНрд╡рд┐рддрд┐ рднрд╛рд╡рдГред рддрдерд╛ рд╕реБрддреНрд░рд╛рддреНрд░рд╛рд╕рдГ рд╕реБрд╖реНрдареБ рддреНрд░рд╛рддрд╛рд░рдГ рд╕реБрдЧреЛрдкрд╛рдГ рд╢реЛрднрдирдЧреЛрдкрд╛рдпрд┐рддрд╛рд░рд╢реНрдЪ рднрд╡рдиреНрддреБ ред рдЙрдкрд╕реНрдерд┐рддреЗрднреНрдпрдГ рд╢рддреНрд░реБрднреНрдпреЛ рд░рдХреНрд╖рдгрдВ рддреНрд░рд╛рдгрдореН ред рддреЗрд╖рд╛рдореБрддреНрдкрддреНрддрд┐рдирд┐рд░реЛрдзреЗрди рд░рдХреНрд╖рдгрдВ рдЧреЛрдкрдирдореН рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay they, Indra, Earth, P┼лс╣гan, Bhaga, Aditi and the five orders of beings, give increase to our habitations; may they be to us granters of happiness, bestowers of food, guides to good, our gracious defenders and preservers.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

They strengthen our earthly realmтАФIndra, Earth, P┼лс╣гan, Bhaga, Aditi, the Five Peoples.
Affording good shelter, good help, good guidance, let them be good herdsmen for us, offering us good protection.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The published translation seems to suggest an etymological relationship between тАЬearthly realmтАЭ and тАЬEarth,тАЭ but in fact they are lexically distinct: kс╣г─Б╠Бma and pс╣Ыthiv─л╠Б, though adjacent.

The list of strengtheners in ab is oddly assorted, but up till the last term they are all divinities or (pс╣Ыthiv─л╠Б) capable of being so configured; I therefore donтАЩt understand the presence of the тАЬfive peoplesтАЭ (p├б├▒ca j├бn─Бс╕е), who are humans. GeldnerтАЩs ref. to X.53.4 is no help (at least to me).

Both Geldner and Renou take the injunc. vardhan as modal тАЬmay they / let them strengthen.тАЭ Certainly the impv. bh├бvantu in the 2nd hemistich would support this interpr., but in general modal readings of injunctives are rather rare.

The 2nd hemistich contains 5 cmpds with su- as first member, all but the last bahuvr─лhis, as Renou points out. The odd-man-out is sugop─Б╠Бс╕е тАШgood herdmenтАЩ. All 5 have accent on the 2nd member.

Griffith

May they, Earth, Aditi, Indra, Bhaga, Pusan increase our laud, increase the Fivefold people.
Giving good help, good refuge, goodly guidance, be they our good deliverers, good protectors.

Geldner

Die m├╢gen unseren Wohnsitz zum Gedeihen bringen: Indra, die Erde, Pusan, Bhaga, Aditi, die f├╝nf V├╢lker; sie sollen uns gute Sch├╝tzer, gute Helfer, gute Weiser, gute Schirmer, gute Hirten sein.

Grassmann

Sie m├╢gen uns st├дrken: Indra, die Erde, der Erdboden, Puschan, Aditi, die f├╝nf Geschlechter; sie m├╢gen uns sch├╢nschirmend, sch├╢n helfend, sch├╢n leitend, sch├╢n sch├╝tzend, sch├╢n beh├╝tend sein.

Elizarenkova

рдЕрдирдпрд╛ рдЛрд╖рд┐рд░рд╛рддреНрдорд╛рдирдВ рдкрд░реЛрдХреНрд╖рд╡рджрд╛рд╣ ред рд╣реЗ рджреЗрд╡рд╛рдГ рднрд╛рд░рджреНрд╡рд╛рдЬрдГ рднрд░рджреНрд╡рд╛рдЬрдЧреЛрддреНрд░рдЬрдГ рд╣реЛрддрд╛ рд╕реНрддреЛрддрд╛ рдЕрдпрдореГрд╖рд┐рдГ рджрд┐рд╡реНрдпрдВ рджрд┐рд╡рд┐ рднрд╡рдВ рд╕рджреНрдорд╛рдирдВ рд╕рджрдирдВ рд╕реНрдерд╛рдирдВ рдиреБ рдХреНрд╖рд┐рдкреНрд░рдВ рдирдВрд╢рд┐ рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдкреНрдиреЛрддреБ ред рддрдерд╛ рд╕реБрдорддрд┐рдВ рд╢реЛрднрдирд╛рдВ рдорддрд┐рдВ рдпреБрд╖реНрдорджреАрдпрд╛рдордиреБрдЧреНрд░рд╣рдмреБрджреНрдзрд┐рдВ рдЪ рдпрд╛рддрд┐ рдпрд╛рдЪрддреЗ ред рдпрд╛рддрд┐рд░реНрдпрд╛рдЮреНрдЪрд╛рдХрд░реНрдорд╛ ред рддрджрд░реНрдердореН рдЖрд╕рд╛рдиреЗрднрд┐рдГ рдЖрд╕реАрдиреИрдГ рд╕рддреНрд░рд╛рд╕рдирдВ рдХреБрд░реНрд╡рджреНрднрд┐рдГ рдорд┐рдпреЗрдзреИрдГ рдореЗрдзреНрдпреИрд░реНрдореЗрдзрд╛рд░реНрд╣реИрдГ рдЕрдиреНрдпрдпрдЬрдорд╛рдиреИрдГ рд╕рд╛рд░реНрдзрдВ рдпрдЬрдорд╛рдирдГ рдпрд╛рдЧрдВ рдХреБрд░реНрд╡рдиреНрдирдпрдореГрд╖рд┐рдГ рд╡рд╕реВрдпреБрдГ рд╡рд╕реВрдирд┐ рдзрдирд╛рдиреНрдпрд╛рддреНрдорди рдЗрдЪреНрдЫрдиреН рджреЗрд╡рд╛рдирд╛рдВ рдЬрдиреНрдо рдЬрдирдВ рд╕рдВрдШрдВ рд╡рд╡рдиреНрдж рд╡рдиреНрджрддреЗ ред рд╕реНрддреМрддрд┐ рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay the preseenter of the oblation, Bharadv─Бja, quickly obtain, gods, a celestial abode, as he solicits your good-will; the instrumental tutor of the ceremony, together with pious associates, desirous of riches, glorifies the assembly of the gods.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

To attain the one whose seat is in heaven, o gods, the Hotar of the Bh─Бradv─Бjas now begs for favor.
Sacrificing with the ritual meals set here, desiring goods, he has extolled the breeds of the gods.

Jamison Brereton Notes

As disc. in the published introduction, this is the final vs. of the first hymn in this composite group and as such summarizes the just-concluded hymn and asks for divine favor, naming the poet, or rather his family.

The grammatical identity and the use of n├бс╣Г┼Ыi is uncertain. Grassmann labels it as an aor. (also Wh Rts), 1st sg. middle, and this interpr. is reflected in GeldnerтАЩs and RenouтАЩs tr. – though both add a modal feature (тАЬm├╢chte ich тАж,тАЭ тАЬje voudrais тАжтАЭ) that would again be somewhat unusual for an injunctive. Lubotsky also groups it with the root aor.

and calls it an injunc. but with ? (By contrast Hoffmann wonтАЩt commit to an analysis [219].) In one sense a finite aor. is the most likely interpr., but if so, we must explain the accent on what appears to be a non-initial main-clause verb. The hemistich would also switch from 1st ps. in this p─Бda to 3rd ps. in the rest of the vs. (bh─Б╠Бradv─Бjaс╕е тАж y─Бti тАж), and though RVic discourse is certainly capable of that, itтАЩs one more anomaly. The published translation follows OldenbergтАЩs preference for LudwigтАЩs interpr. of the form as an infinitive. In either case (finite form or infin.) it is, as Oldenberg says, тАЬauffallend gebildet.тАЭ I take it as a loc. inf. with a purpose function, though I realize that this is ad hoc.

In the context of later ┼Ыrauta ritual, the application of hot─Б╠Бand y├бjam─Бnaс╕е to the same individual would be strange. But the ritual roles so distinct in middle Vedic ┼Ыrauta texts are by no means clearly parceled out in the RV, and in particular y├бjam─Бna- does not usually identify a particular ritual role but acts as an attributive participle, as I think it does here.

Griffith

Come now, O Gods, to your celestial station: the Bharadvajas’ priest entreats your favour.
He, sacrificing, fain for wealth, hath honoured the Gods vath those who sit and share oblations.

Geldner

M├╢chte ich doch zur himmlischen Bewohnerschaft dringen, ihr G├╢tter. Der Opferpriester aus dem Bharadvajageschlecht geht euch um Gunst an. Mit den sitzenden Opfergenossen opfernd hat er das Geschlecht der G├╢tter, Gut begehrend, gelobt.

Grassmann

Nun hat Bharadvadscha den himmlichen Sitz erreicht, o G├╢tter; zu hoher Gunst gelangt er, der Priester; opfernd mit den aufgetragenen Speisen hat er das Geschlecht der G├╢tter nach Gut verlangend verehrt.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬDrive away, Agni, to a distance the wicked, felonious, malignant enemy; grant us felicity, protector of the virtuous.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Away with this crooked, cheating, ill-intentioned thief, o Agni.
Make an easy passage for him far, far away, o lord of settlements.

Jamison Brereton Notes

This first vs. of the extra material has various lexical ties to the first hymn: vс╣Ыjin├бm: 2c vс╣Ыjin─Б╠Б; satpate: 4a s├бtpat─лn; rip├║m: 7d rip├║с╕е, which might help explain why it (and the following two vss.) were attached here.

Geldner attaches daviс╣гс╣нh├бm asya satpate to ab and begins a new cl. with kс╣Ыdh─л╠Б: тАЬSchaffe gute Fahrt.тАЭ I assume that one of his motivations is the accent on kс╣Ыdh─л╠Б, which appears to be in the middle of a p─Бda. And he may feel that making тАЬeasy passageтАЭ (sug├бm) for a criminal would be contrary to expectation. However, he seems to ignore the asya – at least I find nothing in his tr. that corresponds to it. The accentual problem can be easily resolved: the three vss. 13-15 seem to have an 8 8 / 8 4 structure, rather than 8 8 / 12. On this analysis of the meter, kс╣Ыdh─л╠Бstarts a new p─Бda and should be accented. In vs. 14 vс╣Ы╠Бko h├н с╣г├бс╕е is a new clause and nicely fits a separate p─Бda, and in vs. 15 gop─Б╠Бam─Б╠Бis also syntactically separate.

Vs. 15 also supports my interpr. in another way: k├бrt─Б naс╕е тАж sug├бm тАЬmake good passage for usтАЭ is syntactically parallel to my interpr. of 13 тАж asya тАж kс╣Ыdh─л╠Б sug├бm тАЬmake good passage for him,тАЭ with naс╕е corresponding to asya. As for making good passage for a criminal, the point is to get him as far away as fast as possible, and good passage will accomplish this faster than bad.

(RenouтАЩs interpr. is overly complex; though he does find space for the asya, he does not deal with the accented verb. I wonтАЩt treat it further here.)

13-15 ...{Loading}...
Jamison Brereton Notes

As noted in the published introduction, I consider the remaining vss. to belong to a different hymn (or hymns?), appended to the unified, well-structured hymn found in vss. 1-12. Vss. 13-15 are unified by their meter, including an unusual variant of Uс╣гс╣Зih with the configuration 8 8 / 8 4; see disc. ad vs. 13. Whether vs. 16, in Anuс╣гс╣нubh, belongs to this set or was independently appended I donтАЩt know, but it certainly has a тАЬfinalтАЭ feel to it.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThese our grinding stones are anxious, Soma, for your friendship; destroy the voracious Paс╣Зi, for verily he is a wolf.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Jah─л ninatriс╣Зam paс╣Зim vс╣Ыko hi saс╕е: paс╣Зi here means a trader, a greedy trafficker, who gives no offerings to the gods, no presents to the priests; hence, he comes to be identified with an asura, or enemy of the gods;

Vс╣Ыka = a robber, an extortioner, from the root vс╣Ыk, to seize or take away, adane

Jamison Brereton

Surely our pressing stones have bellowed for your
companionship, Soma.
Smash down the rapacious niggard. For he is a wolf!

Jamison Brereton Notes

The unusual position of h├н, normally a 2nd position element, is due to immediately following kam. For whatever reason (and I donтАЩt know it), h├н kam is a phrasal unit, whether it occurs in expected 2nd position (I.98.1, II.28.8, VIII.11.10) or not (VIII.44.24, IX.49.4, X.100.5). II.37.5 may provide a transition between the two, since the h├н kam sequence is not p─Бda-initial there, but it is in 2nd position in its clause.

The standard treatments (Grassmann, Geldner, Renou) take v─Бva┼Ы├║с╕е to тИЪva┼Ы тАШwish forтАЩ, but K├╝mmel (477-80) has argued persuasively that morphological factors favor instead a connection with тИЪv─Б┼Ы тАШbellowтАЩ – though he allows for a secondary contamination from the former root for a sense тАЬsehns├╝chtig br├╝llen.тАЭ I am in complete agreement.

The most salient feature of the pressing stones is their noise, and so bellowing for SomaтАЩs companionship like the bovines that are the usual subjects of тИЪv─Б┼Ы makes perfect sense.

See comm. ad vs. 13 for the four-syllable p─Бda consisting of the nominal sentence vс╣Ы╠Бko h├н с╣г├бс╕е. As I argued in my 2009 тАЬFunction of Animals in the RVтАЭ (Paris animal vol., 206-9, esp. 208), the wolf is a cross-category in RVic classification, and this statement is a quasi-legal declaration that a particular human evil-doer is an outlaw – with parallels in other early Indo-European traditions.

Jamison Brereton Notes

As noted in the published introduction, I consider the remaining vss. to belong to a different hymn (or hymns?), appended to the unified, well-structured hymn found in vss. 1-12. Vss. 13-15 are unified by their meter, including an unusual variant of Uс╣гс╣Зih with the configuration 8 8 / 8 4; see disc. ad vs. 13. Whether vs. 16, in Anuс╣гс╣нubh, belongs to this set or was independently appended I donтАЩt know, but it certainly has a тАЬfinalтАЭ feel to it.

English translation:

тАЬYou are munificent and illustrious, gods, with Indra for your chief, be with us, protectors, on the road, and grant us happiness.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Because you of good drops, with Indra preeminent, are heaven-bound, make good passage for us on the road. (Be) herdsmen at home.

Jamison Brereton Notes

In the second hemistich ├бdhvan тАШon the roadтАЩ and am─Б╠БтАШat homeтАЩ are contrastive, as Renou points out. The brief tag gop─Б╠Бam─Б╠Бmust be a separate clause: both Geldner and Renou supply an imperatival тАЬbe,тАЭ as do I. Again clausal division supports the metrical division suggested ad vs. 13.

13-15 ...{Loading}...
Jamison Brereton Notes

As noted in the published introduction, I consider the remaining vss. to belong to a different hymn (or hymns?), appended to the unified, well-structured hymn found in vss. 1-12. Vss. 13-15 are unified by their meter, including an unusual variant of Uс╣гс╣Зih with the configuration 8 8 / 8 4; see disc. ad vs. 13. Whether vs. 16, in Anuс╣гс╣нubh, belongs to this set or was independently appended I donтАЩt know, but it certainly has a тАЬfinalтАЭ feel to it.

рдкрдиреНрдерд╛рдВ рдкрдиреНрдерд╛рдирдВ рдорд╛рд░реНрдЧрдореН рдЕрдкрд┐ рдЕрдЧрдиреНрдорд╣рд┐ ред рдЕрдкрд┐рдЧрддрд╛рдГ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрддрд╛рдГ рд╕реНрдордГ ред рдХреАрджреГрд╢рдореН ред рд╕реНрд╡рд╕реНрддрд┐рдЧрд╛рдВ рд╕реБрд▓реЗрди рдЧрдиреНрддрд╡реНрдпрдореН рдЕрдиреЗрд╣рд╕рдВ рдкрд╛рдкрд░рд╣рд┐рддрдореНред рдпреЗрди рдкрдерд╛ рдЧрдЪреНрдЫрдиреН рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рд╛рдГ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╛рдГ рджреНрд╡рд┐рд╖рдГ рджреНрд╡реЗрд╖реНрдЯреНрд░реАрдГ рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рдГ рдкрд░рд┐ рд╡реГрдгрдХреНрддрд┐ рдкрд░рд┐рд╡рд░реНрдЬрдпрддрд┐ рдмрд╛рдзрддреЗ рд╡рд╕реБ рдзрдирдВ рдЪ рд╡рд┐рдиреНрджрддреЗ рд▓рднрддреЗ ред рддрд╛рджреГрд╢рдВ рдкрдиреНрдерд╛рдирдорд┐рддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ рее реерезрейрее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWe have travelled along the road prosperously traversed and free from evil, and by which (a man) avoids adversaries and acquires wealth.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

We have gone on the faultless path leading to well-being,
on which one avoids all hatreds and finds goods.

рдЕрдзрд┐рдордиреНрддреНрд░рдореН (VC)
  • рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡реЗрджреЗрд╡рд╛:
  • рдЛрдЬрд┐рд╢реНрд╡рд╛рдГ
  • рдирд┐рдЪреГрджрдиреБрд╖реНрдЯреБрдкреН
  • рдЧрд╛рдиреНрдзрд╛рд░рдГ
рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдлрд┐рд░ рдХреИрд╕реЗ рдорд╛рд░реНрдЧ рд╕рд┐рджреНрдз рдХрд░рдиреЗ рдЪрд╛рд╣рд┐рдпреЗрдВ, рдЗрд╕ рд╡рд┐рд╖рдп рдХреЛ рдХрд╣рддреЗ рд╣реИрдВ рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рд╣реЗ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпреЛ ! (рдпреЗрди) рдЬрд┐рд╕рдХреЛ рд╡реАрд░ рдЬрди (рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рд╛рдГ) рд╕рдм (рджреНрд╡рд┐рд╖рдГ) рд╢рддреНрд░реБрдУрдВ рдХреЛ (рдкрд░рд┐, рд╡реГрдгрдХреНрддрд┐) рд╕рдм рдУрд░ рд╕реЗ рджреВрд░ рдХрд░рддрд╛ рдФрд░ (рд╡рд╕реБ) рдзрди рдХреЛ (рд╡рд┐рдиреНрджрддреЗ) рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реЛрддрд╛ рд╣реИ рдЙрд╕ (рдЕрдиреЗрд╣рд╕рдореН) рди рдирд╖реНрдЯ рдХрд░рдиреЗ рдпреЛрдЧреНрдп рдФрд░ (рд╕реНрд╡рд╕реНрддрд┐рдЧрд╛рдореН) рдЬрд┐рд╕рдореЗрдВ рд╕реБрдЦ рдХреЛ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реЛрддреЗ рдЙрд╕ (рдкрдиреНрдерд╛рдореН) рдорд╛рд░реНрдЧ рдХреЛ рд╣рдо рд▓реЛрдЧ (рдЕрдкрд┐) рднреА (рдЕрдЧрдиреНрдорд╣рд┐) рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реЛрдВ реерезремрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рд░рд╛рдЬрд╛рджрд┐ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдп рдРрд╕реЗ рдорд╛рд░реНрдЧреЛрдВ рдХреЛ рдмрдирд╛рд╡реЗрдВ, рдЬрд┐рдирдореЗрдВ рдЬрд╛рддреЗ рд╣реБрдУрдВ рдХреЛ рдЪреЛрд░реЛрдВ рдХрд╛ рднрдп рди рд╣реЛ рдФрд░ рджреНрд░рд╡реНрдп рдХрд╛ рд▓рд╛рдн рднреА рд╣реЛ реерезремрее рдЗрд╕ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдореЗрдВ рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡реЗ рджреЗрд╡реЛрдВ рдХреЗ рдХрд░реНрдореЛрдВ рдХрд╛ рд╡рд░реНрдгрди рд╣реЛрдиреЗ рд╕реЗ рдЗрд╕ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдХреЗ рдЕрд░реНрде рдХреА рдЗрд╕рд╕реЗ рдкреВрд░реНрд╡ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдХреЗ рдЕрд░реНрде рдХреЗ рд╕рд╛рде рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрддрд┐ рдЬрд╛рдирдиреА рдЪрд╛рд╣рд┐рдпреЗ рее рдпрд╣ рдЗрдХреНрдпрд╛рд╡рдирд╡рд╛рдБ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдФрд░ рддреЗрд░рд╣рд╡рд╛рдБ рд╡рд░реНрдЧ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реБрдЖ рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рд╣реЗ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпрд╛ ! рдпреЗрди рд╡реАрд░реЛ рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рд╛ рджреНрд╡рд┐рд╖рдГ рдкрд░рд┐ рд╡реГрдгрдХреНрддрд┐ рд╡рд╕реБ рд╡рд┐рдиреНрджрддреЗ рддрдордиреЗрд╣рд╕рдВ рд╕реНрд╡рд╕реНрддрд┐рдЧрд╛рдВ рдкрдиреНрдерд╛рдВ рд╡рдпрдордкреНрдпрдЧрдиреНрдорд╣рд┐ реерезремрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдкреБрдирдГ рдХреАрджреГрд╢рд╛ рдорд╛рд░реНрдЧрд╛ рдирд┐рд░реНрдорд╛рддрд╡реНрдпрд╛ рдЗрддреНрдпрд╛рд╣ рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдЕрдкрд┐) (рдкрдиреНрдерд╛рдореН) рдорд╛рд░реНрдЧрдореН (рдЕрдЧрдиреНрдорд╣рд┐) рдЧрдЪреНрдЫреЗрдо (рд╕реНрд╡рд╕реНрддрд┐рдЧрд╛рдореН) рд╕реБрдЦрдВ рдЧрдЪреНрдЫрдиреНрддрд┐ рдпрд╕реНрдорд┐рдБрд╕реНрддрдореН (рдЕрдиреЗрд╣рд╕рдореН) рдЕрд╣рдиреНрддрд╡реНрдпрдореН (рдпреЗрди) (рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рд╛рдГ) рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╛рдГ (рдкрд░рд┐) (рджреНрд╡рд┐рд╖рдГ) рд╢рддреНрд░реВрдиреН (рд╡реГрдгрдХреНрддрд┐) рджреВрд░реАрдХрд░реЛрддрд┐ (рд╡рд┐рдиреНрджрддреЗ) рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдиреЛрддрд┐ (рд╡рд╕реБ) рджреНрд░рд╡реНрдпрдореН реерезремрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рд░рд╛рдЬрд╛рджрд┐рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпрд╛ рдИрджреГрд╢рд╛рдиреН рдорд╛рд░реНрдЧрд╛рдиреН рд╕реГрдЬрдиреНрддреБ рдпреЗрд╖реБ рдЧрдЪреНрдЫрддрд╛рдВ рдЪреЛрд░рднрдпрдВ рди рд╕реНрдпрд╛рджреНрджреНрд░рд╡реНрдпрд▓рд╛рднрд╢реНрдЪ рднрд╡реЗрджрд┐рддрд┐ реерезремрее рдЕрддреНрд░ рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡реЗрджреЗрд╡рдХреГрддреНрдпрд╡рд░реНрдгрдирд╛рджреЗрддрджрд░реНрдерд╕реНрдп рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╛рд░реНрдереЗрди рд╕рд╣ рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрддрд┐рд░реНрд╡реЗрджреНрдпрд╛ рее рдЗрддреНрдпреЗрдХрдкрдЮреНрдЪрд╛рд╢рддреНрддрдордВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдВ рддреНрд░рдпреЛрджрд╢реЛ рд╡рд░реНрдЧрд╢реНрдЪ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрддрдГ рее

рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛ рдЬреЛрд╢реА тЖР рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рдо) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ
